ND State 158-95-16-9-10TFH - Well Evaluation
The Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC.-ND State 158-95-16-9-10TFH [SW
SW Section 16, T158N-R95W] is located approximately 7.3 miles north of Tioga in Williams
County, North Dakota. It will serve to expand McGregor Field, situated along the western flank
of the Nesson anticline (Figure 1). The subject well is a double-section, horizontal Three Forks
well within the Williston Basin consisting of one ~9,809' long lateral drilled to the north
(353.94º). The curve will be kicked off in the Lodgepole and landed within the Three Forks
Formation. Multiple offset wells will be used to land the curve in the appropriate target.
Directional drilling and geo-steering techniques would then be used in tandem to maintain
maximum exposure to the target zone.
Lithology
Lithology descriptions and sample analysis began in the Otter Formation in order to log the top
of the Kibbey Formation.
Select formation tops and marker were used for curve landing
purposes, comparing these tops to select offset well surrounding the surface location (Figure 1).
Figure 1. GIS map of well location, existing wells and fields. (NDIC, GIS map server, 2014)
The top of the Three Forks Formation was logged at 9,644' TVD (-7,159' MSL). The first
bench of the Three Forks Formation was the target reservoir for the lateral portion of the well. It
consists primarily of a light tan to cream colored dolomite exhibiting fine intercrystalline
porosity, interbedded with light blue-green shale and a light brown layer of argillaceous dolomite
low in section (Figure 2). The target zone contained trace to rare amounts of spotty to even light
brown oil staining.
Figure 2. Three Forks Formation (Adam Collar, Sunburst well site geologist).
Curve Landing
Data including rate of penetration (ROP), torque, and lagged samples were used to determine
marker and formation tops during the vertical hole and curve build sections of the well. During
both the vertical and curve, tops were compared to our primary offset wells, in order to ensure a
successful landing in the target zone. The true vertical depth (TVD) of our initial landing target
(9,670' TVD) was calculated by assuming comparable formation thicknesses from the Base Last
Salt marker bed to the proposed landing target. A decision was made to adjust the target to
9,675' TVD after reaching the Lodgepole Formation. A further adjustment was made, dropping
the target landing to 9,679' TVD, after penetrating the Lodgepole "X" marker.
No further
adjustments were made to the landing target after the Lodgepole "X", and directional
successfully landed the curve at 9,678.19' TVD.
Geosteering
The ideal target zone was defined as an 8'
interval, the top of which was initially set at
9,673' TVD, 9' below the top of the Three
Forks Formation. The most useful signature
for
geo-steering
purposes
was
a
superimposed warm gamma marker, reading
70-85 (API) counts, below a cool gamma
marker,
reading
35-40
(API)
counts,
positioned near the middle of the ideal target
zone (Figure 3).
Fig. 3. Offset well (Gohrick 5TFH) w/ target setting.
Offset wells indicated that the Three Forks well would be up-dipping from entry of the formation
to approximately 13,500' MD. At this depth, it was projected the well would begin to turn over
into a down-dip. Due to a misinterpretation in gamma data, the bit penetrated the Lower Bakken
Shale at 14,515' MD. A successful sidetrack at 14,260' MD was utilized to bring the bit back
into the Three Forks. The structure result was a drop of 18' TVD over 9,981', resulting in a gross
apparent down dip of 0.10° (Figure 4). The bottom-hole location is estimated to be 10,009.55'
north & 1,058.15' west of surface location or approximately 241.85' FNL & 47.28' FEL, NE NE
Section 8, T158N, R95W. Geo-steering techniques exposed 100% to the Three Forks Formation
and 32% of uncased borehole to the 8' Three Forks target zone. The well reached a total depth of
19,826' on September 17, 2014.
Figure 4. Cross-sectional interpretation of the ND State 158-95-16-9-10TFH well showing high gamma interbedded
with the cool gamma sections that detailed the target interval. (David Mueller, Sunburst well-site geologist)
Gas Monitoring
Background gas fluctuated between 150 and 2,400 units. A trip gas of 7,450 units was logged at
17,702' MD. Numerous shows greater than 2,000 units were recorded throughout the course of
the lateral. The entire ideal target zone was observed to contain relatively moderate gas
concentrations and consistent oil staining. Gas values were notably higher when drilling in the
middle of the ideal drilling zone (Figure 5).
Liberty Res. Mang. Company, LLC.
Gross apparent dip = -0.10°

(David Mueller, Sunburst well-site geologist)
Summary
The Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC. - ND State 158-95-16-9-10TFH was spud
on August 27, 2014 and reached total depth in 22 drilling days on September 18, 2014. Samples
from the Three Forks target consisted of primarily of gray to tan dolomite interbedded with pale
green shale. The dolomite exhibited traces of fine intercrystalline porosity. Samples showed
visible oil as spotty trace to rare brown oil stain yielding encouraging fluorescent cuts.
Moderate gas shows were present throughout the center of our ideal target zone. The ND State
158-95-16-9-10TFH awaits completion operations to maximize its production potential.
Respectfully submitted,
David Mueller
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
September 18, 2014

ND State 158-95-16-9-10TFH - LITHOLOGY
Rig crews caught 30' sample intervals from 7,170' to 19,826' (TD). Formation tops and lithology markers have
been inserted into the sample descriptions below for reference. Sample descriptions began in the Mississippian
Otter Formation. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. Sample fluorescence cuts are
masked by invert mud through intermediate casing. Quantifiers in order of abundance are trace, rare, occasional,
common and abundant.
Drilling in the Otter Formation [Mississippian Big Snowy Group]
7,170-7,200 SHALE: dark gray, occasional dark-medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture
7,200-7,230 SHALE: dark gray, occasional dark-medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture
7,230-7,260 SHALE: dark gray, occasional dark-medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture
7,260-7,290 SILTSTONE: light pink, tan, light gray to gray-brown, SANDSTONE: light pink, orange-tan, very fine
grained, sub-angular, poorly sorted, friable, earthy texture; rare SHALE: dark gray, occasional dark-medium gray,
firm, blocky, earthy texture
Kibbey Formation [Mississippian, Big Snowy Group]
7,294' MD / 7,263' TVD (-4,778')
7,290-7,320 SILTSTONE: light pink, tan, light gray to gray-brown, SILTY SANDSTONE: light pink, orange-tan,
very fine grained, sub-angular, poorly sorted, friable, earthy texture
7,320-7,350 SILTSTONE: light pink red, tan, light gray to gray-brown; SILTY SANDSTONE: cream-light pink,
orange-tan, very fine grained, sub-angular, poorly sorted, friable, earthy texture; rare SHALE: red, common red-
brown, rare dark gray, soft-firm, blocky, earthy texture
7,350-7,380 SILTSTONE: light pink red, tan, light gray to gray-brown; SANDSTONE: cream-light pink, orange-
tan, very fine grained, sub-angular, poorly sorted, friable, earthy texture; rare SHALE: red, common red-brown, rare
dark gray, soft-firm, blocky, earthy texture
7,380-7,410 SHALE: red orange, blocky, firm-friable; rare SILTSTONE: as above

gray, mudstone-wackestone, microcrystalline, blocky, firm-hard, crystalline
7,440-7,470 LIMESTONE: cream-light gray, mudstone-wackestone, microcrystalline, blocky, firm-hard, crystalline

rarely firm, slightly calcareous, anhydritic, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light brown-
cream, off white, cryptocrystalline, soft, earthy

HORIZONTAL WELL
ND STATE 158-95-16-9-10TFH
SWSW Section 16-158N-95W
Williams County
Well File # 29101
Dear Terry:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24703, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, shall be located
approximately down the north-south axis (500' drilling corridor per Commission policy) and be no closer than the
200' setback from the north & south boundaries within the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 8, 9, 19,
17-T158N-R95W. *The W/2 SW/4 of Section 8 is within both the McGregor and Temple Fields.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Liberty may set conductor on permitted wells only. Effective June 1, 2014, a
covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site
beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back
whenever filtration operations are conducted. LIBERTY RES MNGMT CO must contact NDIC Field
Inspector Tom Delling at 701-770-8660 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 809 W. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well
head is: 10051 N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Terry L. Hoffman
August 8, 2014

Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested
that notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the
Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal
location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are
8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

inaccuracies are not considered when determining compliance with the spacing/drilling unit boundary setback requirement except in the

3. Casing and cementing will be done to protect potentially productive
hydrocarbons, fresh water zones, abnormal pressure zones,
and prospectively valuable mineral deposits.
A. Casing head: 9 5/8" x 11" 5M multi-bowl w/ flange 22" below GL,Initial BOPE test to 5000 psi. unless 9 5/8" is pre set then SOW
Tubing head 11" 5M x 7 1/16" 10M. BOPE test to 5000 psi before drilling out 7" casing shoe.
B. Operators minimum specifications for pressure control equipment are shown on the attached BOP
schematic. After running surface casing and prior to drilling out, blind rams, pipe rams, manifold,
upper and lower kelly cock and safety valve will be pressure tested to 5000 psi. Hydril will be tested
to 2500 psi. Thereafter, the BOPE will be checked daily for mechanical operations and will be noted
in the IADC drilling reports. Before and after running the intermediate casing the BOPE will be tested
in the same manner. BOP will be tested at both high 5000 psi and low pressure to 250 psi.
Gas Buster will be fully rigged up and tested for fluid integrity, using anti-freeze solution
prior to drilling out surface casing.

D. Other Dril ing Considerations & Lessons Learned:
1. Gas Buster- Not to be used for venting off flowline. Divert all flow to gas buster.
2. Lateral Drilling- Minimize DLS.
3. Salt Sections: Tight hole and stuck pipe may occur. Control drill +/-5' and back-ream
as necessary. Spot freshwater only if severely stuck.
4. Do not rotate PDC bit inside 7" casing while displacing well with kill weight fluids.
Ensure bit & motor are in open hole section.
5. Transfer OBM from storage tanks to rig tanks over the shaker screens.
6. CaCL Brine truck to location after running/cmt'g 7 inch csg. To be determined each well.

3. Information on the existing line, to which operator proposes to connect to, including:
a. Maximum current daily capacity of the existing gas line:
5 mmcfd; but with expansion project to increase to 30 mmcfd.
b. Current throughput of the existing gas line:
~5 mmcfd.
c. Anticipated daily capacity of existing gas line at date of first gas sales:
30 mmcfd with completion of planned line upgrade.
d. Anticipated throughput of existing gas line at date of first gas sales:
5 mmcfd ramping up to 12 mmcfd with completion of subject wells.
e. Gas gatherer issues or expansion plans for the area (if known):
Recently expanded Tioga Gas Plant from 110 mmcfd to 250 mmcfd. Plans in place to
expand system in T158N R95W area with additional line to increase capacity to 30
mmcfd.
4. A detailed flow back strategy including:
a. Anticipated date of first production.
January 5, 2015.
b. Anticipated oil and gas rates and duration. If well is on a multi-well pad, include total
for all wells being completed.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates and Duration: Well production rates estimated as 1000
bopd and 2 mmcfd initial production rate average for 30 days with oil rate declining at
80% thereafter.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates and Duration (Multi-Well Pad):
Total production rate for four wells on pad is 4000 BOPD and 8 mmcfd expected initial
production rate average for 30 days with oil rate declining at 80% thereafter .
5. Amount of gas applicant is currently flaring.
a. Statewide percentage of gas flared (total gas flared/total gas produced) for existing
wells producing from the Bakken petroleum system. Note industry target goals are to
reduce flaring to 26% by 9-1-14, 23% by 1-1-15, 15% by 1-1-16, and 10% by 9-1-20:
Statewide percentage of gas flared for existing Liberty operated wells in June 2014 was
9%.
b. Field wide percentage of gas flared:
Fieldwide (McGregor Field) percentage of gas flared for existing Liberty operated wells
in June 2014 was 6%.

6. Alternatives to flaring.
a. Explain specific alternate systems available for consideration:
We have evaluated alternative gas utilization schemes including gas fired power
generation and pad processing to separate gas liquids.
b. Detail expected flaring reductions if such plans are implemented:
Based upon our existing gas connections and proximity to gas gathering lines and the
Tioga Gas Plant, we do not require additional options for flaring reductions.
